==Unified Exponential Power Law according to Beaucage==

[Beaucage 1995]
* [*Beaucage 1995] G. Beaucage, ''Approximations leading to a unified exponential/power-law approach to small-angle scattering'', J. Appl. Cryst., 28:717--728, 1995

 FIGURE DELETED

===Beaucage===

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \begin{split} I_\text{Beaucage}(Q) & \simeq G \exp\left(-\frac{Q^2R_g^2}{3}\right)\\& + B \exp\left(-\frac{Q^2R_{sub}^2}{3}\right) \left( \frac{\left[\mathrm{erf}\left(QkR_g/\sqrt{6}\right)\right]^3}{Q}\right)^P \\& + G_s \exp\left(-\frac{Q^2R_s^2}{3}\right)\\& + B_s       \left( \frac{\left[\mathrm{erf}\left(Qk_sR_s/\sqrt{6}\right)\right]^3}{Q}\right)^{P_s} \end{split}  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

The first term in eq.  describes the large-scale structure of size <math>R_g</math> composed of small subunits of size <math>R_s</math>, captured in the third term. The second term describes the mass-fractal regime with two structural limits. The low-<math>Q</math> limit is at <math>R_g</math> and is described by the error function. The high-<math>Q</math> limit is at <math>R_{sub}</math> and is described by the exponential pre-factor [Beaucage 1995]. The final two terms are for the sub-structural mer unit. Using eq. , scattering from a system with multiple-size-scale features is parameterized. Generally, the high-<math>Q</math> cutoff for the intermediate power law, <math>R_{sub}</math>, is identical to the sub-structural radius of gyration, <math>R_s</math>. The assumption that <math>R_{sub} = R_s</math> should always be true for typical mass fractals. It should be noted that, although eq.  appears cumbersome, no new parameters have been introduced over local fits using exponentials and power laws.

<math>G</math> is the Guinier pre-factor defined above and <math>B</math> is a pre-factor specific to the type of power-law scattering: <math>B</math> is defined according to the regime in which the exponent <math>P</math> falls. Generally, for surface fractals <math>4 > P > 3</math>, for mass fractals <math>P < 3</math> and for diffuse interfaces <math>P>4</math>. For Porod's law, <math>P=4</math> and <math>B = N_p 2\pi \rho_c^2pS_p</math>, where <math>S_p</math>, is the particulate surface area. For a Gaussian polymer, <math>P = 2</math>, and <math>B</math> is given by <math>2G/R_g^2</math>, through a comparison with the Debye form factor  at the high-<math>Q</math> limit as discussed below. The constant, <math>k</math> in , accounts for an approximation involved in the description of the low-<math>Q</math> power-law limit <ref name="beaucage95"/>. This is an empirical constant that has a value of 1 for steep power-law decays, <math>P > 3</math>. For weak power-law decays, <math>k</math> deviates slightly from 1. For polymeric mass fractals of fractal dimension <math>d_f</math> close to 2 (1.5 to 3), <math>k</math> is empirically found to be close to 1.06. Weak deviations are observed between the scattered intensity as calculated using  and exact calculations for values of <math>Q</math> between <math>2\pi/R_g</math> and <math>\pi/R_g</math> in these cases when <math>k = 1</math>. These deviations are reduced to less than 3

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|Beaucage}}:'''
#[{{mono|G}}] <math>G</math> is the Guinier pre-factor of the larger structure 
#[{{mono|B}}] <math>B</math> is a pre-factor specific to the type of power-law scattering: <math>B</math> is defined according to the regime in which the exponent <math>P</math> falls. 
#[{{mono|Gs}}] <math>G_s</math> is the Guinier pre-factor of the smaller structure 
#[{{mono|Bs}}] <math>B_s</math> is a pre-factor specific to the type of power-law scattering: <math>B_s</math> is defined according to the regime in which the exponent <math>P_s</math> falls. 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] large-scale structure 
#[{{mono|Rsub}}] surface-fractal cut-off radius of gyration, <math>R_{sub}</math> defines the high-<math>Q</math> cutoff for the intermediate power law 
#[{{mono|Rs}}] size <math>R_s</math> of small subunits 
#[{{mono|P}}] scaling exponent of the power law assigned to the larger structure <math>R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|Ps}}] scaling exponent of the power law assigned to the smaller structure <math>R_s</math> 

 FIGURE DELETED

===Beaucage 2===

Equation  can be extended to describe an arbitrary number of interrelated structural levels under the generally applicable assumption that <math>R_\text{sub} = R_s</math>,

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \begin{split} I_\text{Beaucage}(Q)  \simeq \sum_{i=1}^n & G_i \exp\left(-\frac{Q^2R_{g,i}^2}{3}\right)\\+ & B_i \exp\left(-\frac{Q^2R_{g,i+1}^2}{3}\right) \left( \frac{\left[\mathrm{erf}\left(Qk_iR_{g,i}/\sqrt{6}\right)\right]^3}{Q}\right)^{P_i} \end{split}  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

In , <math>i= 1</math> refers to the largest-size structural level. Extensions, such as eq. , can only be justified when data extend over many decades in <math>Q</math>. Eq.  introduces no new parameters over local Guinier and power-law fits.

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|Beaucage2}}:'''
#[{{mono|G_i}}] <math>G_i</math> is the Guinier pre-factor 
#[{{mono|B_i}}] <math>B_i</math> is a pre-factor specific to the type of power-law scattering: <math>B_i</math> is defined according to the regime in which the exponent <math>P_i</math> falls. 
#[{{mono|Rg_i}}] large-scale structure <math>R_{g,i}</math> 
#[{{mono|Rg_i+1}}] size <math>R_{g,i+1}</math> of smaller subunits 
#[{{mono|k_i}}] This is an empirical constant that has a value of 1 for steep power-law decays, <math>P > 3</math>. For weak power-law decays, <math>k</math> deviates slightly from 1 
#[{{mono|k_i+1}}] This is an empirical constant that has a value of 1 for steep power-law decays, <math>P_s > 3</math>. For weak power-law decays, <math>k_s</math> deviates slightly from 1 
#[{{mono|P_i}}] scaling exponent of the power law assigned to the larger structure <math>R_{g,i}</math> 
#[{{mono|P_i+1}}] scaling exponent of the power law assigned to the smaller structure <math>R_{g,i+1}</math> 

 FIGURE DELETED

==WormLikeChainEXV==

[Pedersen 1996]
* [*Pedersen 1996] J. S. Pedersen and P. Schurtenberger, ''Scattering functions of semiflexible polymers with and without excluded volume effects'', Macromolecules, 29:7602--7612, 1996

 FIGURE DELETED

This form factor calculates the form factor for a flexible cylinder with a circular cross section and a uniform scattering length density. The non-negligible diameter of the cylinder is included by accounting for excluded volume interactions within the walk of a single cylinder. Inter-cylinder interactions are NOT included. The function calculated has been given by [Pedersen 1996]. The model "Method 3 With Excluded Volume" is used, which is a parametrization of simulations of a discrete representation of the worm-like chain model of Kratky and Porod applied in the pseudo-continuous limit.



\ \underline{Input Parameters for model {{mono|WormLikeChainEXV}}:}\  
#[{{mono|R}}] radius <math>R</math> of cylindrical core with uniform scattering length density 
#[{{mono|l}}] Kuhn length\footnote{The Kuhn length <math>l</math> is related to the length <math>a</math> of locally stiff segment simply via <math>l=2a</math>} <math>l</math> of semi-flexible worm-like structure 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length <math>L</math> of semi-flexible worm-like structure 


 FIGURE DELETED



==KholodenkoWorm==

 FIGURE DELETED

* [*Kholodenko 1993] A. L. Kholodenko, ''Analytical calculation of the scattering function for polymers of arbitrary flexibility using the dirac propagator'', Macromolecules, 26:4179--4183, 1993

[Kholodenko 1993] presented a new approach using the analogy between Diracs fermions and semi-flexible polymers. The form factor <math>P_0(Q)</math> resulting from Kholodenkos approach is designed to reproduce correctly the rigid-rod limit and the random-coil limit. Defining <math>x = 3L/l</math> (<math>L</math>: contour length, <math>l</math>: Kuhn length), it is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_0(Q,L,l) &= \frac{2}{x} \left[I_{(1)} -\frac{1}{x}I_{(2)}\right]  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} I_{(n)}(x) &= \int_0^x  f(z) \, z^{n-1} \, dz \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

together with

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} f(z)) &= \begin{cases} \displaystyle \frac{1}{E}\frac{\sinh(Ez)}{\sinh(z)} & \text{for} \quad \displaystyle Q \leq \frac{3}{l}\\\\displaystyle \frac{1}{F}\frac{\sin(Fz)}{\sinh(z)} & \text{for} \quad \displaystyle Q > \frac{3}{l} \end{cases} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

and

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} E = \sqrt{1-\left(\frac{lQ}{3}\right)^2} \quad \text{and} \quad F = \sqrt{\left(\frac{lQ}{3}\right)^2-1} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

For flexible cylinders with a circular cross section and a uniform scattering length density the cross section form factor is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_{cs} = \left(2 \frac{J_1(QR)}{QR}\right)^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

so that the overall form factor is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P(Q,L,l,R) = P_0(Q,L,l)\, P_{cs}(Q,R) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|KholodenkoWorm}}:'''
#[{{mono|R}}] radius <math>R</math> of cylindrical core with uniform scattering length density 
#[{{mono|l}}] Kuhn length\footnote{The Kuhn length <math>l</math> is related to the length <math>a</math> of locally stiff segment simply via <math>l=2a</math>} <math>l</math> of semi-flexible worm-like structure 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length <math>L</math> of semi-flexible worm-like structure 

 FIGURE DELETED



==Diblock copolymer micelles==

 FIGURE DELETED


* [*Pedersen 1996] J. S. Pedersen and M. C. Gerstenberg, ''Scattering form factor of block copolymer micelles'', Macromolecules, 29(4):1363--1365, 1996
* [*Pedersen 2000] J.S. Pedersen, ''Form factors of block copolymer micelles with spherical, ellipsoidal and cylindrical cores'', J. Appl. Cryst., 33:637--640, 2000
* [*Svaneborg 2002] C. Svaneborg and J.S. Pedersen, ''Form factors of block copolymer micelles with excluded-volume interactions of the corona chains determined by monte carlo simulations'', Macromolecules, 35:1028--1037, 2002

For block copolymers, which form micelles, several form factor have been implemented [Pedersen 1996] [Pedersen 2000] [Svaneborg 2002] for spherical, ellipsoidal, and cylindrical shapes. It has been assumed that one unit is forming the core of the micelles and the other the corona. The core is assumed to have a homogeneous scattering length density, but may contain some amount of solvent. For the polymer chains in the corona either a model where Gaussian chains are attached to the core or a corona model of semi-flexible interacting self-avoiding chains (only for spherical core) or a continuous model, where a radial profile of the form <math>\Phi(r)\varpropto r^{-\alpha}</math> has been assumed. The form factors have been parameterized such, that the excess scattering of the corona and the core are consistent with the composition and density of the two separate block units of the copolymer.

===Micelles with a homogeneous core and Gaussian chains on the surface===

It is assumed that the diblock copolymer consist of a block unit for which the solvent is poor and a block unit with is good. The insoluble blocks form a relatively compact core whereas the soluble blocks form a diffuse corona surrounding the core. The form factor of a micelle contains four different terms: the self-correlation term of the core <math>N_\text{agg}^2\beta_\text{core}^2\,P_\text{core}(q)</math>, the self-correlation term of the chains <math>N_\text{agg}\beta_\text{brush}^2\,P_\text{brush}(q)</math>, the cross-term between the core and chains <math>2N_\text{agg}^2\beta_\text{core}\beta_\text{brush}\,S_\text{brush-core}(q)</math>, and the cross term between different chains <math>N_\text{agg}(N_\text{agg}-1)\beta_\text{brush}^2\,S_\text{brush-brush}(q)</math>. It can be written (Pedersen \& Gerstenberg, 1996)

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} I_\text{mic}    &= N_\text{agg}^2\beta_\text{core}^2\,P_\text{core}(q) + N_\text{agg}\beta_\text{brush}^2\,P_\text{brush}(q) \\&+ 2N_\text{agg}^2\beta_\text{core}\beta_\text{brush}\,S_\text{brush-core}(q) + N_\text{agg}(N_\text{agg}-1)\beta_\text{brush}^2\,S_\text{brush-brush}(q) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

<math>N_\text{agg}</math> is the aggregation number of diblock polymers forming the micelle and <math>\beta_\text{brush}=V_\text{brush}(\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})</math> and <math>\beta_\text{core}=V_\text{core}(\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})</math> the excess scattering length of a block in the corona and in the core, respectively. <math>V_\text{brush}</math> and <math>V_\text{core}</math> are the total volume of a block in the corona and in the core. <math>\eta_\text{brush}</math> and <math>\eta_\text{core}</math> are the corresponding scattering length densities and <math>\eta_\text{solv}</math> is the scattering length density of the surrounding solvent. The functions <math>P_\text{core}(q)</math>, <math>P_\text{brush}(q)</math>, <math>S_\text{brush-core}(q)</math>, and <math>S_\text{brush-brush}(q)</math> are all 1 for <math>q=0</math>. The definitions of these four functions depend on the shape of the core and are given below.



====Spherical core:====

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{core}(q,R_\text{core}) &= \Phi^2(qR_\text{core})\\\Phi(qR) &= 3\frac{\sin(qR)-qR\cos(qR)}{(qR)^3} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{brush}(q,R_g)&= 2\frac{\exp(-x)-1+x}{x^2} \text{ with } x = R_g^2q^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-core}(q,R_\text{core},Rg,d) &= \Phi(qR_\text{core})\psi(qR_g)\frac{\sin(q[R_\text{core}+dR_g])}{q[R_\text{core}+dR_g]}\\\psi(qRg) &= \frac{1-\exp(-x)}{x} \text{ (form factor amplitude of the chain)} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-brush}(q,R_\text{core},d,R_g) &= \psi^2(qR_g)\left[\frac{\sin(q[R_\text{core}+dR_g])}{q[R_\text{core}+dR_g]}\right]^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

For micelles with a spherical core a few different parameterizations have been implemented {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)}}, {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}. The parameters they all have in common are:  
#[<math>V_\text{brush}</math>] molecular volume the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{core}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the core 
#[<math>\eta_\text{brush}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{solv}</math>] scattering length density of the solvent 
#[<math>x_\text{solv,core}</math>] volume fraction of solvent in the micellar core 
#[<math>R_g</math>] radius of gyration of the block unit in the corona 
#[<math>d</math>]  non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 

For the model {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] radius of the micellar core 
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] grafting density (number of copolymer molecules <math>N_\text{agg}</math> per surface are <math>S</math>, <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math>) 

In contrast to the form factor {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} this one does not necessary consist of copolymers. The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number needed in eq.  are than given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} N_\text{agg} &= n_\text{agg} S \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where the surface of the core is given by <math>S=4\pi R_\text{core}^2</math>. Together with the core volume  <math>V =\frac{4}{3}\pi R_\text{core}^3</math> one gets for the excess scattering lengths

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core} &= \frac{V (1-x_\text{solv,core})}{N_\text{agg}} (\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv}) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 

For the model {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Rc}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] core radius 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number in eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\N_\text{agg} &= (1-x_\text{solv,core}) \frac{4}{3}\pi R_\text{core}^3  / V_\text{core} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Rc}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 

For the model {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>N_\text{agg}</math>] aggregation number 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and the core radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> needed in eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\R_\text{core} &= \left( \frac{N_\text{agg} V_\text{core}}{1-x_\text{solv,core}} \, \frac{3}{4\pi}\right)^{1/3} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}:'''
#[{{mono|N_agg}}] aggregation number 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 

====ellipsoidal core with semi-axis <math>(R,R,\epsilon R)</math>:====

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{core}(q,R_\text{core},\epsilon) &= \int_0^{\pi/2}\Phi^2[qr(R_\text{core},\epsilon,\alpha)] \, \sin\alpha \, d\alpha\\\text{with } \, r(R_\text{core},\epsilon,\alpha) &= R_\text{core}\sqrt{\sin^2\alpha+\epsilon^2\cos^2\alpha} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{brush}(q,R_g)&= 2\frac{\exp(-x)-1+x}{x^2} \text{ with } x = R_g^2q^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-core}(q,R_\text{core},\epsilon,Rg,d) &= \psi(qR_g)\int_0^{\pi/2} \Phi(qr(\dots))\frac{\sin(q[r(\dots)+dR_g])}{q[r(\dots)+dR_g]} \, \sin\alpha \, d\alpha \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-brush}(q,R_\text{core},d,R_g) &= \psi^2(qR_g) \int_0^{\pi/2}\left[\frac{\sin(q[r(\dots)+dR_g])}{q[r(\dots)+dR_g]}\right]^2 \, \sin\alpha \, d\alpha \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

As for micelles with spherical core also for those with an ellipsoidal core several parameterizations have been implemented {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)}}, {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}. The parameters they all have in common are:  
#[<math>V_\text{brush}</math>] molecular volume the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{core}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the core 
#[<math>\eta_\text{brush}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{solv}</math>] scattering length density of the solvent 
#[<math>x_\text{solv,core}</math>] volume fraction of solvent in the micellar core 
#[<math>R_g</math>] radius of gyration of the block unit in the corona 
#[<math>d</math>]  non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[<math>\epsilon</math>] eccentricity of the ellipsoidal micelle <math>(R_\text{core},R_\text{core},\epsilon R_\text{core})</math> 

For the model {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] radius of the micellar core <math>(R_\text{core},R_\text{core},\epsilon R_\text{core})</math> 
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] grafting density (number of copolymer molecules <math>N_\text{agg}</math> per surface are <math>S</math>, <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math>) 

In contrast to the form factor {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} this one does not necessary consist of copolymers. The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number needed in eq.  are given by {{eqn|<math>\begin{align} N_\text{agg} &= n_\text{agg} S \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where the surface of the core is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S  &= \begin{cases} 2\pi R_\text{core}^2 \left(1+\frac{\text{arctanh}(\sin({\ae}))}{\sin({\ae})}\right)& \text{for } \epsilon < 1\\2\pi R_\text{core}^2 \left(1+\frac{\ae}{\tan({\ae})}\right) & \text{for } \epsilon \geq 1 \end{cases}\\{\ae} &= \begin{cases} \arccos(\epsilon) & \text{for } \epsilon < 1\\\arccos(1/\epsilon) & \text{for } \epsilon \geq 1 \end{cases} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

Together with the core volume <math>V =\frac{4}{3}\pi \epsilon R_\text{core}^3</math> one gets for the excess scattering lengths

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core} &= \frac{V (1-x_\text{solv,core})}{N_\text{agg}} (\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv}) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''underline{Input Parameters for model {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|epsilon}}] eccentricity of the ellipsoidal micelle <math>(R_\text{core},R_\text{core},\epsilon R_\text{core})</math> 

For the model {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Rc}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] core radius 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number in eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\N_\text{agg} &= (1-x_\text{solv,core}) \frac{4}{3}\pi \epsilon R_\text{core}^3  / V_\text{core} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Rc}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|epsilon}}] eccentricity of the ellipsoidal micelle <math>(R_\text{core},R_\text{core},\epsilon R_\text{core})</math> 

For the model {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>N_\text{agg}</math>] aggregation number 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and the core radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> needed in eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\R_\text{core} &= \left( \frac{N_\text{agg} V_\text{core}}{1-x_\text{solv,core}} \, \frac{3}{4\pi\epsilon}\right)^{1/3} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ELL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}:'''
#[{{mono|N_agg}}] aggregation number 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|epsilon}}] eccentricity of the ellipsoidal micelle <math>(R_\text{core},R_\text{core},\epsilon R_\text{core})</math> 

====cylindrical core with radius R<sub>core</sub> and height H====

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{core}(q,R_\text{core},H) &= \int_0^{\pi/2}\Psi^2(q,R_\text{core},H,\alpha) \, \sin\alpha \, d\alpha\\\text{with } \, \Psi(q,R_\text{core},H,\alpha) &= \frac{2J_1(qR_\text{core}\sin\alpha)}{qR_\text{core}\sin\alpha} \frac{\sin(qH/2\, \cos\alpha)}{qH/2\, \cos\alpha} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

and <math>J_1(x)</math> is the first order Bessel function of the first kind.

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{brush}(q,R_g)&= 2\frac{\exp(-x)-1+x}{x^2} \text{ with } x = R_g^2q^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-core}(q,& R_\text{core},H,Rg,d) = \psi(qR_g) \quad \times\\& \int_0^{\pi/2} \Psi(q,R_\text{core},H,\alpha) \Xi(q,R+dR_g,H+2dR_g,\alpha) \, \sin\alpha \, d\alpha \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where <math>\Xi(q,R_\text{core},H,\alpha)</math> is the form factor amplitude of the shell:

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \Xi(q, R_\text{core} H,\alpha)  &= \biggl[ \frac{R}{R_\text{core}+H} \frac{2J_1(qR_\text{core}\sin\alpha)}{qR_\text{core}\sin\alpha} \cos(qH/2\, \cos\alpha)\\&+ \frac{H}{R_\text{core}+H} J_0(qR_\text{core}\sin\alpha) \frac{\sin(qH/2\, \cos\alpha)}{qH/2\, \cos\alpha} \biggr] \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where <math>J_0(x)</math> is the zeroth order Bessel function of the first kind.

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-brush}(q,& R_\text{core},H,d,R_g) = \psi^2(qR_g) \quad \times\\&\int_0^{\pi/2} \Xi^2(q,R_\text{core}+dR_g,H+2dR_g,\alpha)\, \sin\alpha \, d\alpha \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

As for micelles with spherical core also for those with a cylindrical core several parameterizations have been implemented {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)}}, {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}. The parameters they all have in common are: \sloppy  
#[<math>V_\text{brush}</math>] molecular volume the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{core}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the core 
#[<math>\eta_\text{brush}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{solv}</math>] scattering length density of the solvent 
#[<math>x_\text{solv,core}</math>] volume fraction of solvent in the micellar core 
#[<math>R_g</math>] radius of gyration of the block unit in the corona 
#[<math>d</math>]  non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[<math>H</math>] height of the cylindrical core of the micelle 

For the model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] radius of the micellar core <math>(R_\text{core},R_\text{core},\epsilon R_\text{core})</math> 
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] grafting density (number of copolymer molecules <math>N_\text{agg}</math> per surface are <math>S</math>, <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math>) 

In contrast to the form factor {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} this one does not necessary consist of copolymers. The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number needed in eq.  are than given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} N_\text{agg} &= n_\text{agg} S \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where the surface of the core is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S  &= 2\pi R_\text{core} H \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

Together with the core volume <math>V =\pi R_\text{core}^2 H</math> one can calculate the excess scattering lengths by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core} &= \frac{V (1-x_\text{solv,core})}{N_\text{agg}} (\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv}) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|H}}] height of the cylindrical core of the micelle 

For the model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Rc}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] core radius 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number in eq.  are than given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\N_\text{agg} &= (1-x_\text{solv,core}) \pi  R_\text{core}^2 H  / V_\text{core} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Rc}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|H}}] height of the cylindrical core of the micelle 

For the model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>N_\text{agg}</math>] aggregation number 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and the core radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\R_\text{core} &= \sqrt{ \frac{N_\text{agg} V_\text{core}}{1-x_\text{solv,core}} \, \frac{1}{\pi H}} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}:'''
#[{{mono|N_agg}}] aggregation number 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|H}}] height of the cylindrical core of the micelle 

====wormlike micelles with cylindrical cross-section with radius R<sub>core</sub>, Kuhn-length l and contour length L:====

The form factors for a worm-like micelles are approximated by the form factor of the Kholodenko-worm according to section  where the scattering length density profile across the worm segments are described by those of a rod-like micelle . The corresponding function in eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{core}(q,R_\text{core},l,L) &= P_\text{worm}(q,l,L) P_\text{cs}(q,R_\text{core},d,R_g)  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

the contribution of the worm-like conformation of the micelle <math>P_\text{worm}(q,l,L)</math> is described by the formula of Kholodenko for worm-like structures given in eq. . The contribution of the cross-section <math>P_\text{cs}</math> is the same as for rod-like micelles and given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{cs}(q,R_\text{core},d,R_g) &= \left[ \frac{2J_1(qR_\text{core})}{qR_\text{core}} \right]^2\\\text{Si}(x) &= \int_0^x \, t^{-1} \sin t\, dt \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{brush}(q,R_g)&= 2\frac{\exp(-x)-1+x}{x^2} \text{ with } x = R_g^2q^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-core}(q,& R_\text{core},l,L,Rg,d) = \psi(qR_g) \quad \times\\& \frac{2J_1(qR_\text{core})}{qR_\text{core}} J_0[q(r_\text{core}+dR_g)]  P_\text{worm}(q,l,L) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-brush}(q,R_\text{core},l,L,d,R_g) &= \psi^2(qR_g) J_0^2[q(r_\text{core}+dR_g)]  P_\text{worm}(q,l,L) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

As for micelles with spherical core also for those worm-like micelles several parameterizations have been implemented {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)}}, {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)_nagg}}. The parameters they all have in common are: \sloppy  
#[<math>V_\text{brush}</math>] molecular volume the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{core}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the core 
#[<math>\eta_\text{brush}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{solv}</math>] scattering length density of the solvent 
#[<math>x_\text{solv,core}</math>] volume fraction of solvent in the micellar core 
#[<math>R_g</math>] radius of gyration of the block unit in the corona 
#[<math>l</math>] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 
#[<math>L</math>] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 

For the model {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] radius of the micellar core 
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] grafting density (number of copolymer molecules <math>N_\text{agg}</math> per surface are <math>S</math>, <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math>) 

In contrast to the form factor {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)_Rc}} and {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)_nagg}} this one does not necessary consist of copolymers. The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number needed in eq.  are than given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} N_\text{agg} &= n_\text{agg} S \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where the surface of the core is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S  &= 2\pi R_\text{core} L \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

Together with the core volume <math>V =\pi R_\text{core}^2 L</math> one can calculate the excess scattering lengths by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core} &= \frac{V (1-x_\text{solv,core})}{N_\text{agg}} (\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv}) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|l}}] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 

For the model {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)_Rc}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] core radius 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number in eq.  are than given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\N_\text{agg} &= (1-x_\text{solv,core}) \pi  R_\text{core}^2 L  / V_\text{core} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Rc}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|l}}] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 

For the model {{mono|WORM+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} the other parameters are  
#[<math>N_\text{agg}</math>] aggregation number 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and the core radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\R_\text{core} &= \sqrt{ \frac{N_\text{agg} V_\text{core}}{1-x_\text{solv,core}} \, \frac{1}{\pi L}} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}:'''
#[{{mono|N_agg}}] aggregation number 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|l}}] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length of the worm-like of the micelle 

====micelles with rod-like core:====

The form factors for micelles with a rod-like core are an approximations of the form factors of micelles with a cylindrical core where <math>H\gg R_\text{core}+d R_g</math>. The corresponding function in eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{core}(q,R_\text{core},H) &= P_H(q,H) P_\text{cs}(q,R_\text{core},d,R_g)  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

with

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_H(q,H)    &= 2\text{Si}(qH)/(qH) - 4 \sin^2(qH/2)/(q^2H^2)\\P_\text{cs}(q,R_\text{core},d,R_g) &= \left[ \frac{2J_1(qR_\text{core})}{qR_\text{core}} \right]^2\\\text{Si}(x) &= \int_0^x \, t^{-1} \sin t\, dt \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{brush}(q,R_g)&= 2\frac{\exp(-x)-1+x}{x^2} \text{ with } x = R_g^2q^2 \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-core}(q,& R_\text{core},H,Rg,d) = \psi(qR_g) \quad \times\\& \frac{2J_1(qR_\text{core})}{qR_\text{core}} J_0[q(r_\text{core}+dR_g)] P_H(q,H) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} S_\text{brush-brush}(q,R_\text{core},H,d,R_g) &= \psi^2(qR_g) J_0^2[q(r_\text{core}+dR_g)] P_H(q,H) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

As otherwise the definitions of the geometry for rod-like micelles are mainly the same than for cylindrical micelles only the list of input parameters are given here. There is only one difference in the model {{mono|ROD+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} compared to the model {{mono|CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg}} and that is that for rod-like structures always the grafting density of polymer chains on the surface of the core is used, i.e. <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math> instead of <math>N_\text{agg}</math>. For the model {{mono|ROD+Chains(RW)_nagg}} this means that the core radius has to be calculated by <math>R_\text{core} = 2 n_\text{agg} V_\text{core} / (1-x_\text{solv,core})</math>

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ROD+Chains(RW)}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|H}}] height of the rod-like core of the micelle 

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ROD+Chains(RW)_Rc}}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|H}}] height of the rod-like core of the micelle 

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ROD+Chains(RW)_nagg}}:'''
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in core 
#[{{mono|Rg}}] gyration radius of polymer chains in the corona 
#[{{mono|d}}] This value should be around 1. Non-penetration of the chains into the core is mimicked by <math>d\sim 1</math> for <math>R_\text{core}\gg R_g</math> 
#[{{mono|H}}] height of the rod-like core of the micelle 

===Micelles with a homogeneous core and a corona with decaying density profile of the form <math>\varphi(r)\varpropto r^{-\alpha}</math>===

 FIGURE DELETED

The structure of block copolymer micelles may be described in terms of the model of starlike polymer as proposed by [Daoud and Cotton 1982].

* [*Daoud and Cotton 1982] M. Daoud and J.P. Cotton, ''Star shaped polymers - a model for the conformation and its concentration-dependence'', Journal de Physique (Paris), 43:531, 1982

Starlike polymers consist of a homogeneous, dense polymer core surrounded by a polymer layer. As a consequence of the spherical or cylindrical geometry, the density profile <math>\phi(r)</math> in the polymer layer decreases according to [Wijmans and Zhulina] as

* [*Wijmans and Zhulina] C. M. Wijmans and E. B. Zhulina, ''Polymer brushes at curved surfaces'', Macromolecules, 26:1214--7224, 1993

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \phi(r) \begin{cases} \phi_\text{core}    & \text{for } r < R_\text{core}\\\phi_\text{brush} \left(\frac{r}{R_\text{core}}\right)^{-\alpha} & \text{for } R_\text{core} \leq r \leq R_\text{core}+t\\0                  & \text{for } r > R_\text{core}+t \end{cases}  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

with <math>\alpha =(D-1)(3\nu-1)/(2\nu)</math>. <math>D</math> is determined by the dimension of the curvature of the grafted surface (spherical <math>D=3</math>, cylindrical <math>D=2</math>, planar <math>D=1</math>). <math>\nu</math> is the Flory exponent, which has characteristic values as given in Table . The corresponding density profile is schematically shown in Figure . Micelles consist of a well-defined micellar core with a radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> and a micellar shell or corona extending to the outer micellar radius <math>R_m=R_\text{core}+t</math>, where <math>t</math> is the thickness of the corona.

 TABLE DELETED

For a given radial profile according to eq.  the form factor of spherical micelle can be calculated by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} F_\text{SPHERE} &= \int_0^\infty 2\pi r^2 \phi(r) \frac{\sin(qr)}{qr}\,dr \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

In case of a rod-like micelle the form factor can be separated in two terms <math>I(q) = P_H(q)P_\text{cs}(q)</math> as already in shown in eq. . The cross-term contribution to the scattering intensity is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \begin{split} P_\text{cs}(q) &=  F_\text{cs}^2(q)\\F_\text{cs}(q) &=  \int_0^\infty 2\pi r \phi(r) J_0(q)\,dr \end{split} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

However, as it is more convenient here to formulate the scattering intensity in terms of excess scattering length of the block units in the core <math>\beta_\text{core}</math> and the corona <math>\beta_\text{brush}</math> like in eq.  the form factor is split into two parts, the form factor of the homogeneous core <math>F_\text{core}(q)</math> and the form factor of the corona <math>F_\text{brush}(q)</math>. The overall scattering intensity <math>I(q)</math> is than given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \begin{split} I(q) &=   N_\text{agg}^2\beta_\text{core}^2 F_\text{core}^2(q) + 2 N_\text{agg}^2\beta_\text{core}\beta_\text{corona} F_\text{core}(q) F_\text{corona}(q)\\& +   N_\text{agg}(N_\text{agg}-1) \beta_\text{corona}^2 F_\text{corona}^2(q) +   N_\text{agg} P_\text{brush}(q) \end{split}  \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

The excess scattering length of a block in the corona and in the core, respectively, <math>\beta_\text{brush}=V_\text{brush}(\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})</math> and <math>\beta_\text{core}=V_\text{core}(\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})</math> are defined in the same way than in eq. . <math>V_\text{brush}</math> and <math>V_\text{core}</math> are the total volume of a block in the corona and in the core. <math>\eta_\text{brush}</math> and <math>\eta_\text{core}</math> are the corresponding scattering length densities and <math>\eta_\text{solv}</math> is the scattering length density of the surrounding solvent. <math>F_\text{core}(q)</math> is the form factor of the core and normalized to 1 for <math>q=0</math>. Also the form factor of the corona <math>F_\text{corona}(q)</math> and the form factor of the local fluctuations in the corona originating from the individual chains <math>P_\text{brush}(q)</math> are normalized to 1 for <math>q=0</math>. Similar to section  models for spherical and rod-like shapes have been implemented which are described in the following paragraphs.

====spherical core:====

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} F_{core}^2(q,R) &= 3\frac{\sin(qR)-qR\cos(qR)}{(qR)^3} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} F_\text{brush}(q,R,t)&= \frac{1}{C_{norm}} \int_{R_\text{core}}^{R_\text{core}+t} 2\pi r^2 r^{-\alpha} \frac{\sin(qr)}{qr} \, dr \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

with

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} C_{norm} &= \begin{cases} \frac{4}{3-\alpha} \pi \left(\left(R_\text{core}+t\right)^{3-\alpha} - R_\text{core}^{3-\alpha}\right) & \text{for } \alpha \neq 2\\4\pi\ln\left(\frac{R_\text{core}+t}{R_\text{core}}\right) & \text{for } \alpha = 2 \end{cases} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

For the scattering contribution of the individual chains in the corona <math>P_\text{brush}</math> the scattering function for worm-like chains with excluded volume and negligible cross-section, contour length <math>L</math> and Kuhn-length <math>b</math> according to section  has been implemented.

For micelles with a spherical core a few different parameterizations have been implemented {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a}, {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc} and {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg}.

The parameters they all have in common are:  
#[<math>V_\text{brush}</math>] molecular volume the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{core}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the core 
#[<math>\eta_\text{brush}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{solv}</math>] scattering length density of the solvent 
#[<math>\alpha</math>] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[<math>t</math>] corona thickness 
#[<math>L</math>] contour length of the chain in the corona 
#[<math>b</math>] Kuhn-length of the chain in the corona 

For the model {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] radius of the micellar core 
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] grafting density (number of copolymer molecules <math>N_\text{agg}</math> per surface are <math>S</math>, <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math>) 

In contrast to the form factor {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc} and {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg} this one does not necessary consist of copolymers. The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} N_\text{agg} &= n_\text{agg} S \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where the surface of the core is given by <math>S=4\pi R_\text{core}^2</math>. Together with the core volume  <math>V =\frac{4}{3}\pi R_\text{core}^3</math> one gets for the excess scattering lengths

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core} &= \frac{V (1-x_\text{solv,core})}{N_\text{agg}} (\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv}) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|alpha}}] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[{{mono|t}}] corona thickness 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length of the chain in the corona 
#[{{mono|b}}] Kuhn-length of the chain in the corona 

For the model {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] core radius 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number for eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\N_\text{agg} &= (1-x_\text{solv,core}) \frac{4}{3}\pi R_\text{core}^3  / V_\text{core} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|alpha}}] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[{{mono|t}}] corona thickness 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length of the chain in the corona 
#[{{mono|b}}] Kuhn-length of the chain in the corona 


For the model {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg} the other parameters are  
#[<math>N_\text{agg}</math>] aggregation number 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and the core radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> needed for eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\R_\text{core} &= \left( \frac{N_\text{agg} V_\text{core}}{1-x_\text{solv,core}} \, \frac{3}{4\pi}\right)^{1/3} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg}:'''
#[{{mono|N_agg}}] aggregation number 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|alpha}}] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[{{mono|t}}] corona thickness 
#[{{mono|L}}] contour length of the chain in the corona 
#[{{mono|b}}] Kuhn-length of the chain in the corona 


====rodlike core:====

In case of a rod-like micelle the form factor can be separated in two terms <math>I(q) = P_H(q)P_\text{cs}(q)</math> as already in shown in eq. . The cross-term contribution to the scattering intensity is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \begin{split} P_\text{cs}(q) &=  F_\text{cs}^2(q)\\F_\text{cs}(q) &= \int_0^\infty 2\pi r \phi(r) J_0(qr)\,dr = F_\text{cs,core}(q)+F_\text{cs,brush}(q) \end{split} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

The contribution of the homogeneous core is given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} F_\text{cs,core}(q) = \frac{2 J_1(qR_c)}{qR_c} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

and for the corona by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} F_\text{cs,brush}(q) &=\frac{1}{c_\alpha}\int_{R_c}^{R_c+t} 2\pi r \, r^{-\alpha} J_0(qr)\,dr \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} c_\alpha &= \int_{R_c}^{R_c+t} 2\pi r \, r^{-\alpha}\,dr \\&= \begin{cases} 2\pi\ln\left(\frac{R_c+t}{R_c}\right)                                   & \text{ for } \alpha = 2  \\\frac{2}{2-\alpha} \pi \left((R_c+t)^{2-\alpha}-R_c^{2-\alpha}\right)   & \text{ for } \alpha \neq 2 \end{cases} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

For the scattering contribution of the individual chains in the corona <math>P_\text{local}</math> normally can be neglected for rod-like micelles in contrast to spherical structures as for structures with a lower dimension than spheres, this contribution becomes more and more negligible. To account for the scattering of the individual chains at least in first approximation and without introducing new parameters a form factor similar to the one of star polymers has been implemented.

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} P_\text{local}(q) &= \frac{\Gamma(\mu)}{qt} \frac{\sin\left(\mu \arctan(q t)\right)}{\left(1+q^2t^2\right)^{\mu/2}}\\\mu &=\frac{1}{\nu}-1 ,\quad \alpha = \frac{3\nu-1}{2\nu} \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \mu = 2(1-\alpha) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

The form factor to describe the scattering of the individual chains is identical to the blob scattering contribution in star-like polymers according to Dozier (). The exponential damping length <math>\xi</math> in the definition of the star polymer has been set to the shell thickness <math>t</math>. In the original paper of Pedersen the <math>P_\text{local}</math> was described by the scattering of a semi-flexible chain with excluded volume according to section , which however would require to define two more parameters.

For micelles with a rod-like core a few different parameterizations have been implemented {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a}, {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc} and {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg}.

The parameters they all have in common are:  
#[<math>V_\text{brush}</math>] molecular volume the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{core}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the core 
#[<math>\eta_\text{brush}</math>] scattering length density of the diblock copolymer part forming the corona 
#[<math>\eta_\text{solv}</math>] scattering length density of the solvent 
#[<math>x_\text{solv,core}</math>] amount of solvent in the core 
#[<math>\alpha</math>] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[<math>t</math>] corona thickness 
#[<math>H</math>] height of the cylinder 

For the model {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] radius of the micellar core 
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] grafting density (number of copolymer molecules <math>N_\text{agg}</math> per surface are <math>S</math>, <math>n_\text{agg}=N_\text{agg}/S</math>) 

In contrast to the form factor {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc} and {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg} this one does not necessary consist of copolymers. The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} N_\text{agg} &= n_\text{agg} S \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

where the surface of the core is given by <math>S=2\pi R_\text{core}H</math>. Together with the core volume  <math>V =\pi R_\text{core}^2H</math> one gets for the excess scattering lengths

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core} &= \frac{V_\text{core} (1-x_\text{solv,core})}{N_\text{agg}} (\eta_\text{core}-\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv}) \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of a block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in the core 
#[{{mono|alpha}}] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[{{mono|t}}] corona thickness 
#[{{mono|H}}] rod height 

For the model {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc} the other parameters are  
#[<math>R_\text{core}</math>] core radius 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and aggregation number for eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\N_\text{agg} &=  2\pi R_\text{core}^2H   \, \frac{1-x_\text{solv,core}}{V_\text{core}} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Rc}:'''
#[{{mono|R_core}}] core radius 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in the core 
#[{{mono|alpha}}] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[{{mono|t}}] corona thickness 
#[{{mono|H}}] rod height 

For the model {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_Nagg} the other parameters are  
#[<math>n_\text{agg}</math>] specific aggregation number, aggregation number per surface area 
#[<math>V_\text{core}</math>] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core  The excess scattering lengths and the core radius <math>R_\text{core}</math> needed for eq.  are given by

{{eqn|<math>\begin{align} \beta_\text{core}  &= V_\text{core}  (\eta_\text{core} -\eta_\text{solv})\\\beta_\text{brush} &= V_\text{brush} (\eta_\text{brush}-\eta_\text{solv})\\R_\text{core} &=  \frac{2 n_\text{agg}\, V_\text{core}}{1-x_\text{solv,core}} \end{align}</math>|dummy}}

'''Input Parameters for model {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a_nagg}:'''
#[{{mono|n_agg}}] specific aggregation number (number of chains per surface area) 
#[{{mono|V_core}}] molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar core 
#[{{mono|V_brush}}]  molecular volume of single block unit in the micellar corona 
#[{{mono|eta_core}}] scattering length density of spherical core 
#[{{mono|eta_brush}}] scattering length density of the block unit in the corona 
#[{{mono|eta_solv}}] scattering length density of solvent 
#[{{mono|xsolv_core}}] amount of solvent in the core 
#[{{mono|alpha}}] exponent of the radial scattering length density profile (<math>r^{-\alpha}</math>) 
#[{{mono|t}}] corona thickness 
#[{{mono|H}}] rod height

</ref><ref name="MuellerDelsanti2000"> F. M\"uller, M. Delsanti, L. Auvray, J. Yang, Y.J. Chen, J.W. Mays, B. Demé, M. Tirrell, , and P. Guenoun. Ordering of urchin-like charged copolymer micelles: Electrostatic, packing and polyelectrolyte correlations. ''Eur. Phys. J. E'', 3:45--53, 2000.
