</ref> three-body interactions are at least considered in first approximation and they find for the scattering intensity the expression \begin{eqnarray} \overline{I(Q)} &=& N\, \left\{\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2} + {\left\vert \right\vert}{\overline{F(Q)}}^2 \, \frac{\chi(Q)}{\frac{V}{N}\, (2\pi)^{-3/2} - \chi(Q)} \right\} \\\mbox{with    } \chi(Q) &=& \sqrt{\frac{2}{\pi}} \int_0^\infty dr\, \left[ e^{-U(r)/kT} - 1\right]\, r^2\, \frac{\sin Qr}{Qr} . \end{eqnarray} For a simple hard sphere model with the interaction potential <math>U(r) = \left\{ {  0 \mboxriptsize  for r > 2 R \atop \infty \mboxriptsize  for r \leq 2 R} \right. </math> the scattering intensity can be calculated analytically. According to Raman's theory Debye calculates for the scattering intensity of spheres with a radius <math>R</math> and a volume <math>V_P</math> the expression

{{eqn|<math> \overline{I(Q)} = N\, K^2(QR)\, \left\{ 1 - 8\, N\, \frac{V_P}{V}\, K(2QR) \right\}, </math>|dummy}}

whereby <math>K(x)</math> is the scattering function of a sphere given in appendix . Following the theory of Born and Green one gets a similar expression

{{eqn|<math> \overline{I(Q)} = N\, K^2(QR)\, \left\{ 1 + 8\, N\, \frac{V_P}{V}\, K(2QR) \right\}^{-1}. </math>|dummy}}

Nonetheless both theories are only valid for monodisperse systems of scatterer. In practice, however, most scattering systems have a more or less pronounced size distribution and frequently also an additional variety of shapes. For such systems the interaction potential can not be expressed in a closed form. One has to introduce for each pair of particle type a separate potential <ref name="scatt97"> N. W. Ashcroft and L. Lenker. Structure and resistivity of liquid metals. ''Physical Review'', 145(1):83--90, May 1966.

</ref> which complicates the analytical treatment a lot.

===Isolate particles===

A system of isolate particles is characterized by its property that the positions of a particle is not influenced by the positions of any other particle. For this case the interaction potential <math>U(r)</math> and consequently also  <math>\chi(Q)</math> is identical zero. Therefore the expression for the scattering intensity simplifies to

{{eqn|<math> I(Q) = N\, \overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2} \quad \mbox{or} \quad  I({\underline{ Q}}) = \sum_{i=1}^{N} {\left\vert \right\vert}{F_i({\underline{ Q}})}^2 . </math>|dummy}}

The total scattering intensity is simply the sum of the intensity scattered by the individual particles. A system of non-interacting particles can be realized by diluting the system. Thereby the average distance between the particles is increased and the interaction potential becomes negligible small and does not influence anymore the arrangement of the scatterer.

===Polydisperse System of isolated particles===

The scattering function of a polydisperse system of isolated particles is determined by the shape and size of the particles. In a scattering experiment it is not possible to separate both quantities at the same time. In the data analysis one has to assume one of the quantities either the shape or the size distribution to get then the other quantity. Normally the shape is assumed whereby the size distribution is than obtained from the scattering curve <ref name="scatt75"> O. Glatter. Data evaluation in small angle scattering: Calculation of the radial electron density distribution by means of indirect {Fourier} transformation. ''Acta Physica Austriaca'', 47:83--102, 1977.

</ref><ref name="scatt121"> C. G. Vonk. On two methods for determination of particle size distribution functions by means of small-angle x-ray scattering. ''J. Appl. Cryst.'', 9:433--440, 1976.

</ref>. To get an information about the shape one normally need a system of identical particles, like for example a system of identical proteins. An additional but known size distribution would smear out the scattering too much to still allow to extract confidential information about the particle shape. The scattering intensity of a system of isolated particles of different shape and a size distribution is given by

{{eqn|<math> I({\underline{ Q}}) = \sum_{\mu=1}^M \int N_{\mu}(R) \, \overline{{\left\vert \right\vert}{F_{\mu}(Q,R)}^2} \, dR ,  </math>|dummy}}

whereby <math>N_{\mu}(R)</math> is the size distribution of particles of type <math>\mu</math> and  <math>F_{\mu}(Q,R)</math> its form factor. Form factor of simple objects are listed in appendix  and frequently used size distributions in appendix .

==Influence of <math>N(R)</math> and <math>F(Q,R)</math> on interparticle interferences==

Interparticle interferences in small angle scattering signals have been described in eq.   and  by

{{eqn|<math> \overline{I(Q)}                 = N\,\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2} \left\{1 + \frac{{\left\vert \right\vert}{\overline{F(Q)}}^2}{\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2}} \, (S(Q)-1) \right\}  </math>|dummy}}

Hereby <math>S(Q)</math> describes the influence of the relative arrangement of the scatterers on <math>\overline{I(Q)}</math> and can be calculated by the interaction potential between the scattering particles (eq. ). Interparticle interferences depends next to the relative arrangement also on the square of the average form factor {\small <math>\vert{\overline{F(Q)}}\vert^2</math>}. Only for the case of identical and spherical symmetric scatterer the relation {\small <math>\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2} \equiv \vert{\overline{F(Q)}}\vert^2</math>} is valid. In this case the interparticle interferences only depends on <math>S(Q)</math>. For particles with an irregular shape, however, the two averages are different and depends both on the size distribution as well as on the particle shape and their orientation distribution. For such systems the condition for the derivation the relation from Prins and Zernicke  namely the independency of orientation and size for higher concentrations is not anymore fulfilled. This condition allowed in eq.  to separate the averaging of the particle positions from the averaging of the form factor. Nevertheless the principle influence of a irregular particle shape and a size distribution can be made clear by the means of eq. . For judging their influence the ratio {\small <math>\vert{\overline{F(Q)}}\vert^2/\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2}</math>} is considered.

Taking for example a system of identical but random oriented rotational ellipsoids with the half axis <math>R</math>, <math>R</math>, <math>\nu R</math> the ratio of the two averages is shown in figure  together with the scattering intensity {\small <math>\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2}</math>} of the corresponding ideal dilutes system. The derivation of the formula for calculating  {\small <math>\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2}</math>} and {\small <math>\vert{\overline{F(Q)}}\vert^2</math>} are given in appendix . The figure shows that the ratio decreases for larger scattering vectors <math>Q</math> the more the shaper of the rotational ellipsoid is different from the ideal spherical case (<math>\nu=1</math>). An irregular particle shape already is sufficient to reduce the influence interparticle interferences.

Accordingly also the particle size distribution give rise to a difference in the averages {\small <math>\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2}</math>} and {\small <math>\vert{\overline{F(Q)}}\vert^2</math>}. Figure b shows the ratio of the two averages of spherical scatterers with a lognormal size distribution of different width as a function of <math>Q</math>.  For <math>Q=0</math> the ratio is given by {\small <math>\vert{\overline{F(Q)}}\vert^2/\overline{{\left\vert F(Q)\right\vert}^2} = \exp(-9\sigma^2)</math>}. One can see that the width of the size distribution strongly reduces the interference effect <ref name="scatt151"> P. van Beurten and A. Vrij. Polydispersity effects in the small-angle scattering of concentrated solutions of colloidal spheres. ''J. Chem. Phys.'', 74(5):2744--2748, March 1981.

</ref>.

In general one can say that each kind of disorder reduces interferences. The disorder can have its origin in a random arrangement of particles (dilute systems), in an orientation distribution of irregular shaped particles, or also in a size distribution. 
 FIGURE DELETED

==Scattering laws and structural parameter==

In this section a series of useful scattering laws are presented, which are useful for a simple analysis of experimental data and which allow an easy determination of structural parameters. <ref name="book:Guinier:Fournet"/>.

===Porod volume===

The ratio of the scattering intensity in forward direction <math>I(Q=0)=N\, V_P^2\, \Delta\eta^2</math> and the scattering invariant  <math>\tilde Q = 2\pi^2\Delta\eta^2\, V\, f_p(1-f_p)</math> can be used to determine the particle volume <math>V_P</math> (<math>V</math> describes the illuminated sample volume). <math>f_p\, V = N\, V_P</math> corresponds to the total volume of all scatterers whereby the particle volume <math>V_P</math> can be calculated by

{{eqn|<math> \frac{V_P}{1-f_p} \, \stackrel{f_p \ll 1}{\simeq} \,  V_P = 2\pi^2\, \frac{I(Q=0)}{\tilde Q} . </math>|dummy}}

The measurement of the scattering curve in relative units is therefore sufficiant to determine the volume of a homogeneous scatterer. Sources of errors for this way of determination of particle sizes are the extrapolation into forward direction und more important the extrapolation to large scattering angles (<math>Q^{-4}</math>-extrapolation). Furthermore for large volume fractions <math>f_p</math> the particle volume has to be eventually corrected by a prefactor <math>1/(1-f_p)</math> which is not always known.

===Radius of gyration and Guinier approximation===

The scattering intensity for small angles can be approximated in a series expansion by replacing the expression <math>\frac{\sin Qr}{Qr}</math> in eq.  by a McLaurin series which leads to

{{eqn|<math> I(Q) = V\, \int 4\pi\, r^2\, \gamma(r)\, \left[1-\frac{Q^2r^2}{3!} + \frac{Q^4r^4}{5!} - \dots \right] \, dr \quad , </math>|dummy}}

i.e. <math>I(Q)</math> is expanded by moments <math>\overline{r^n}</math> of <math>\gamma(r)</math>. The first term corresponds to the scattering intensity of <math>Q=0</math>. For the second term Guinier and Fournet <ref name="book:Guinier:Fournet"/> have shown, that it can be related to the gyration radius of the scattering length density <math>R_G</math> by

{{eqn|<math> V\,\int 4\pi\, r^2\, \frac{Q^2r^2}{3!}\, \gamma(r)\, dr = I(0)\, \frac{Q^2R_G^2}{3} \quad \Rightarrow \quad I(Q) = I(0) \, \left( 1-\frac{Q^2R_G^2}{3} \right) </math>|dummy}}

with <math>R_G^2 = \int \eta(r)\, r^2\, dr/\int \eta(r)\, dr</math>. Up to the term of <math>Q^4</math> this series expansion at the beginning of the scattering curve is identical to the series expansion of an exponential function which than leads to the well known Guinier approximation

{{eqn|<math> I(Q) = I(0)\, e^{-Q^2R_G^2/3} .  </math>|dummy}}

The Guinier law is valid for any particle shape which is roughly isodiametric. For flat or elongated structures the Guinier law has to be corrected slightly <ref name="book:Feigin:Svergun"> L. A. Feigin and D. I. Svergun. ''Structure Analysis by Small-Angle X-ray and Neutron Scattering''. Plenum Press, 1987.

</ref><ref name="book:Guinier:Fournet"/>. The radius of gyration for a sphere with radius <math>R</math> is given by <math>R_G=\sqrt{3/5}\, R</math>. The Guinier law is valid in the scattering vector interval <math>0<Q<1/R_G</math>.

===Correlation length===

Another characteristic quantity, which can be easily extracted from the scattering curve <math>I(Q)</math> is the correlation length <math>l_c</math>. The correlation length is defined as the average width of the correlation function  <math>\gamma(r)</math>:

{{eqn|<math> l_c = \frac{2}{\gamma(0)}\, \int \gamma(r) \, dr . </math>|dummy}}

Together with the definition of the scattering invariant <math>\tilde Q</math> in eq.  and the relation between <math>I(Q)</math> and <math>\gamma(r)</math> in eq.  this results after a short calculation (changing of integrations) to

{{eqn|<math> l_c = \pi\, \frac{\int Q\, I(Q)\, dQ}{\int Q^2\, I(Q)\, dQ} \quad . </math>|dummy}}

A sphere with radius <math>R</math> has therefore a correlation length of <math>l_c = \frac{3}{2}\, R</math>.

===Porod law and specific surfaces===

The Porod law describes the scattering behavior at large <math>Q</math> values. As the scattering intensity <math>I(Q)</math> and the correlation function <math>\gamma(r)</math> are related via the Fourier transformation the intensity <math>I(Q)</math> is determined at large values of <math>Q</math> mainly by <math>\gamma(r)</math> at small <math>r</math>. For small <math>r</math>  the correlation function <math>\gamma(r)</math> can be expanded in a Taylor series and one gets according to Guinier and Fournet <ref name="book:Guinier:Fournet"/>

{{eqn|<math> \frac{\gamma(r)}{\gamma(0)} = 1 - \frac{1}{4} \, \frac{S}{V} + \dots \quad ,  </math>|dummy}}

whereby <math>S</math> is the total surface of all scatterer in the illuminated sample volume <math>V</math>. Eq.  together with  result for large <math>Q</math> values into the Porod law

{{eqn|<math> I(Q) \longrightarrow \Delta\eta^2\, \frac{2\pi\, S}{Q^4} .  </math>|dummy}}

A scaling of the scattering intensity on <math>\tilde Q</math> provides an expression for the specific surface <math>S/V</math> of

{{eqn|<math> \lim_{Q\rightarrow \infty} \, \pi\,\frac{I(Q)}{\tilde Q}\, Q^4\, f_p\, (1-f_p) = \frac{S}{V} .  </math>|dummy}}

The Porod law can be applied to all systems having sharp interfaces. \chapter{Experimental Setup of a Small Angle Scattering Instrument}

\chapter{Data Reduction in SAS}

==Correction and Normalization of SANS-Raw data==

A detector of a small angle scattering camera measures the superposition of intensities of different origin:


# Background noise <math>I_B</math> 
# Scattering of the empty sample holder <math>I_{H}</math> 
# scattering of the isolated sample <math>I_S</math>  Furthermore the detector elements can have different efficiencies <math>\epsilon_i</math>. To determine the differential cross-section of of the sample all the different contribution to the total scattering intensity have to be considered and determined separately by different measurements. The quantity to be known is the scattering contribution of the isolated sample <math>I_S</math>, which in general can not be measured directly. Experimental accessible scattering contributions are the scattering of the sample in the sample holder <math>I_{S+H}</math>, the contribution of the empty sample holder <math>I_{H}</math> and the background noise <math>I_B</math>. From this experimental accessible data the wanted scattering contribution of the isolated sample has to be determined.

==Contribution of the isolated sample==

The intensity of the incident beam will be attenuated by absorption and scattering effects within the sample. Also the scattered neutrons will be further attenuated on their residual path through the sample. The measured intensity in a detector element  <math>i</math> is given by

{{eqn|<math> I^0_{S,i} = \int^d_0 dx\, \Phi_0\, \Delta \Omega_i\, \epsilon_i\, e^{-\alpha\,x}\, A\, \rho \, e^{-\frac{\alpha(d-x)}{\cos\theta}} \left\{ \frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d\Omega} + \frac{d\sigma_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega} \right\} . </math>|dummy}}

Hereby <math>d</math> describes the sample thickness in cm, <math>\Phi_0</math> the incident neutron flux in neutrons per cm<math>^2\times</math>sec, <math>d\Omega_i</math> is the solid angle of the detector element <math>i</math> in steradian, <math>\epsilon_i</math> the detection efficiency of detector element <math>i</math> and <math>\alpha</math> the extinction coefficient of the sample in cm<math>^{-1}</math>. <math>A</math> the illuminated sample area in cm<math>^2</math>. <math>\theta</math> describes the angle between the wave vector  <math>'''k'''_0</math> of the incident neutrons and the wave vector <math>'''k'''</math> of the scattered neutrons. <math>\frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d\Omega}</math> and <math>\frac{d\sigma_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega}</math> are the coherent and incoherent differential cross-sections, respectively. For small angle scattering <math>\cos\theta \simeq 1</math> and one yields after integration

{{eqn|<math> I^0_{S,i} = \Phi_0\, \Delta \Omega_i\, \epsilon_i\, \underbrace{A\, \rho \,d}_{N_S}\, \underbrace{e^{-\alpha d}}_{T_S} \left\{ \frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d\Omega} + \frac{d\sigma_{inc}}{d\Omega} \right\} . </math>|dummy}}

The quantity <math>N_S = A\, \rho\, d</math> corresponds to the number of scattering atoms and <math>T_S = e^{-\alpha\, d} = \frac{I_{\rm trans}}{I_0}</math> to the transmissions coefficient, which can be determined from the ration of the intensity of the transmitted primary beam <math>I_{\rm trans}</math> and the intensity of the incident beam <math>I_0</math>. The incoherent scattering is isotropically and equally distributed over the whole solid angle of  <math>4\pi</math>. Therefore one gets for <math>I^0_{S,i}</math>

{{eqn|<math> I^0_{S,i} = \Phi_0\, \Delta \Omega_i\, \epsilon_i\, \left\{ N_S\, T_S \, \frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d\Omega} + A\, \frac{1-T_S}{4\, \pi} \right\} .  </math>|dummy}}

==Correction for sample holder and background noise==

The scattering intensity of an isolated sample can practically never measured directly. The scattering of the sample is always superposed by scattering from the sample holder and by background noise. Background noise is meant to be electronic noise, cosmic radiation, and detection of neutrons, which have not passed through the sample like scattered neutrons from neighboring experiments. Because of this reasons additional measurements have to be carried out, which are a measurement of the empty sample holder <math>I_H</math> and a measurement with a strong absorber like Cadmium in front of the sample to measure the background noise <math>I_B</math>. Together with the measurement of the sample in the sample holder <math>I_{S+H,i}</math> the scattering of the isolated sample <math>I^0_{S,i}</math> on the detector element <math>i</math> can be calculated by

{{eqn|<math> I_{S,i}^0 = \left( \frac{I_{S+H,i}}{M_{S+H}} - \frac{I_{B,i}}{M_B} \right) - \frac{T_{S+H}}{T_H} \left(\frac{I_{H,i}}{M_{H}} - \frac{I_{B,i}}{M_B} \right) .  </math>|dummy}}

The index <math>B</math> stands for \underline{b}ackground, <math>H</math> for the empty sample \underline{h}older, <math>S+H</math> for the sample in the sample holder and <math>S</math> for the scattering of the isolated sample. All intensities have to be normalized on the number of incident neutrons. This can be done for example by division of the measured intensity my a monitor count rate <math>M</math>. The factor <math> \frac{T_{S+H}}{T_H}</math> takes account for the attenuation of the beam by the sample.

The differential cross-section in eq.  can now be calculated from the measurable intensities in eq. . Nevertheless the quantities <math>\Phi_0</math>, <math>\Delta\Omega_i</math> and <math>\epsilon_i</math> still have to be known. Furthermore <math>I_S^0</math> is not given in physical standard units but in units per monitor count. All this can be overcome by a comparison with a standard substance <math>St</math>. Common standard materials are in general materials with a small coherent cross-section and a large incoherent cross-section like vanadium or water. For both of these materials the coherent cross-section is negligible small. The scattering intensities of the standard materials have to be corrected in the same way than the sample itself according to eq. . The ratio of both intensities <math>I^0_{S,i}/I^0_{St,i}</math> leads to

{{eqn|<math> \frac{I^0_{S,i}}{I^0_{St,i}} = \frac{T_S\, N_S\, \displaystyle \left(\frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d \Omega} + \frac{d\sigma_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega} \right)}{T_{St}\,N_{St}\, \displaystyle \frac{d\sigma^{St}_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega}} </math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math> \Leftrightarrow \qquad \displaystyle \frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d\Omega} + \frac{d\sigma_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega} = \frac{I^0_{S,i}}{I^0_{St,i}} \, \frac{T_{St}\, N_{St}}{T_S\, N_S}\, \displaystyle \frac{d\sigma^{St}_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega} </math>|dummy}}

{{eqn|<math> \displaystyle \mbox{or}\qquad \frac{d\sigma_{\rm coh}}{d\Omega} + \frac{d\sigma_{\rm inc}}{d\Omega} = \frac{I^0_{S,i}}{I^0_{St,i}} \, \frac{(1-T_{St})\, \displaystyle \frac{A_{St}}{4\pi}}{T_S\, N_S} . </math>|dummy}}

If water is used as a standard the last formula has to be multiplied on the right side with an empirical factor <math>f(\lambda,\sigma_t,T) \simeq 1</math>. This factor corrects for the different efficiencies of the detector for different neutron energies. This correction can become important in case of water because of it inelastic scattering behavior.

==Correction and normalization of SAXS raw data==

In the future the modules {{mono|sasfit_sd}}, {{mono|sasfit_sq}}, {{mono|sasfit_ff}} and {{mono|sasfit_peaks}} will be converted to external plugins. 
# Added {{mono|sasfit_peaks}}, a new class of model functions containing peaks. 
# Added capability to ship {{sasfit}} as standalone executable, allows running on system without the need of external libraries (e.g. Tcl, BLT, ...)  \item[4.03.2008] ({{sasfit}} version 0.87) The last modification in the menu navigation still had bugs. Hopefully they are removed in this version. \item[28.02.2008] ({{sasfit}} version 0.86) The menu navigation has been debugged and optimized. Corrected a bug in calculating the polydispersity index (PDI) in DLS cumulant analysis (PDI=Gamma2/Gamma1<math>\hat{ }</math>2) \item[25.01.2008] ({{sasfit}} version 0.85) A bug for the form factors  {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a*} has been corrected. The implementation of the scaling approximation, partial structure factors and local monodisperse approach has been improved. \item[9.01.2008] ({{sasfit}} version 0.84) Form factor for worm-like micelles ({{mono|WORM+Chains(RW), WORM+Chains(RW)_Rc, WORM+Chains(RW)_Nagg}}) and for cluster aggregates ({{mono|Mass Fractal (Exp(-x) Cut-Off), Fisher-Burford, MassFractExp,MassFractGauss, Mass Fractal (Exp(-x<math>\hat{ }}</math>a) Cut-Off), DLCAggregation, RLCAggregation, MassFractOverlappingSph} have been implemented. Furthermore a simple scheme for importing data from the clipboard has been implemented, which e.g. allows to copy/paste data from spread-sheets directly into {{sasfit}}. Corrected a bug for the form factors  {{mono|ROD+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a*} \item[4.10.2007] ({SPHERE+Chains(RW), SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Rc, SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Nagg{{sasfit}}} version 0.80) Next to the correction of some bugs a simulation option for multiple data sets has been implemented. Furthermore an option has been implemented to subtract a theoretical scattering contribution from the experimental data set, like e.g. a constant background signal. The format of the project files have up to now never been tested for compatibility. An attempt has been started to change this for the future versions. \item[20.8.2007] A couple of form factors for spherical, elliptical, cylindrical and very long rod-like micelles consisting of a homogeneous core and which are either grafted with Gaussian chains {{mono|*(RW)*}}, or grafted with semi-flexible self-avoiding and interacting chains {{mono|*(SAW)*}} or a corona with a power-law decaying profile <math>r^{-\alpha}</math> {{mono|*(R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a)*} have been implemented: {{mono| SPHERE+Chains(RW), SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Rc, SPHERE+Chains(RW)_Nagg, SPHERE+Chains(SAW), SPHERE+Chains(SAW)_Rc, SPHERE+Chains(SAW)_Nagg, SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }}</math>-a, SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }</math>-a_Rc, SPHERE+R<math>\hat{ }</math>-a_Nagg, ELL+Chains(RW), ELL+Chains(RW)_Rc, ELL+Chains(RW)_Nagg, CYL+Chains(RW), CYL+Chains(RW)_Rc, CYL+Chains(RW)_Nagg, ROD+Chains(RW), ROD+Chains(RW)_Rc, ROD+Chains(RW)_nagg, ROD+R<math>\hat{ }</math>-a, ROD+R<math>\hat{ }</math>-a_Rc, ROD+R<math>\hat{ }</math>-a_nagg } \item[30.6.2007] Rudimental copy algorithm to copy plots or parameters into window-clipboard. Everything is copied in wmf-format and the option only works fine for information in non-scrolled widgets. Copy-option can be activated with right mouse button or double click of left mouse button. A triaxial ellipsoidal ({{mono|triaxEllShell}}) shell with semiaxis {{mono|a}}, {{mono|b}}, {{mono|c}} and shell thickness {{mono|t}} is available. \item[4.6.2007] Implementation of form factors for cylindrical shells with circular cross-section and capped ends ({{mono|CylShell2}}) and without capped ends ({{mono|CylShell1}}) together with an approximation for very long cylindrical shells ({{mono|LongCylShell}}) \item[27.3.2007] Implementation of form factors for bi-continuous systems ({{mono|TeubnerStrey}} and {{mono|DAB}}) \item[23.2.2007] Implementation of the structure factor for a system of charged, spheroidal objects in a dielectric medium according to the RMSA model of Hayter and Penfold \item[11.11.2006]  Implementation of a semiflexible polymer according to Kholodenko, some form factors with plane geometry, which are intended to be used with lamellar structure factors ({{mono|homogenousXS}}, {{mono|TwoInfinitelyThinPlates}}, {{mono|LayeredCentroSymmetricXS}}, {{mono|BiLayerGauss}}), a sphere with Gaussian chains attached {{mono|SphereWithGaussChains}} and a slightly different parametrised form factor named {{mono|BlockCopolymerMicelle}}. An additional option for reading ASCII data files is now available, which allows to convert values for the scattering vector from nm<math>^{-1}</math> into Å<math>^{-1}</math> and vice versa. \sloppy \item[23.10.2006] Implementation of a polydsiperse star {{mono|PolydisperseStar}} and of flexible ring polymers {{mono|FlexibleRingPolymer}} and {{mono|mMemberedTwistedRing}}. \item[22.10.2006] Implementation of the form factor of a flexible polymer with Gaussian statistics (in different parameterisations \verb"Gauss", \verb"Gauss2", \verb"Gauss3") for a polydisperse flexible polymer with Gaussian statistics (\verb"GaussPoly") and a flexible ring of polymer with Gaussian statistics (\verb"FlexiblePolymerRing") \item[12.10.2006] Under the menu option \verb"Calc/DLS..." next to a cumulant fit also a double stretched exponential decay can be selected to fit dynamic light scattering data. \item[5.10.2006] Implementation of a spherical shell with a diffuse (expontential) scattering length density profile inside the shell caused by solvent penetration into the shell \item[13.9.2006] Implementation of a form factor for spheres with gaussian chains attached. \item[19.7.2006] First release (current version: 0.71) at the moment only a windows version is available. The installation files for tcl/tk and blt are included in the distribution file.
